## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target is a time-derivative of population size, dP_dt, modeled from time t and population P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth ODEs (density-independent and density-dependent, with possible time-varying environment or harvesting). Typical relationships express per-capita growth as a function of P and/or t, then multiply by P to obtain dP_dt.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent growth/decline)
- Linear birth–death balance: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (immigration/emigration plus net per-capita growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; logistic expanded form)
- Higher-order crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (stronger-than-quadratic density limitation)
- Logistic differential form (carrying capacity via inverse K): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (approach to carrying capacity K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density-dependence curvature via exponent)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases with log(P))
- Ricker-type continuous limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with exponential density feedback plus mortality)
- Allee effect (weak/strong depensation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P and at high P)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality added to density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (harvest or extra mortality proportional to population)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removal independent of P)
- Seasonally forced per-capita growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environmental forcing of growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (seasonal resources): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4))) (K(t) varying periodically through the density-feedback term)
- Secular environmental trend in growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P - c2 * P**2 (gradual change in intrinsic growth with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita formulation: many models take (dP_dt)/P = g(P,t); this implies dP_dt often contains an overall factor P.
- Carrying-capacity behavior: if dP_dt has a factor (1 - c*P), then P = 1/c is a stable equilibrium (growth changes sign there).
- Crowding signatures: negative P**2 (or higher powers) terms indicate density-dependent limitation; the lowest-order diagnostic is dP_dt vs P becoming concave downward.
- Allee-effect signatures: additional low-P root (e.g., factor (c*P - 1)) creates a threshold below which dP_dt < 0, implying extinction risk at small P.
- Harvesting decomposition: subtracting c*P corresponds to proportional harvest/mortality; subtracting a constant corresponds to quota/constant-yield removal and can create a critical population size where recovery fails.
- Gompertz vs logistic discrimination: presence of P*log(c/P) implies log-linear decline of per-capita growth with P, often fitting populations approaching an asymptote with asymmetric trajectories.
- Seasonality/forcing: sinusoidal dependence on t typically enters by modulating intrinsic growth c0 or density-feedback strength, producing periodic oscillations in dP_dt even if P is steady.
- Multiple equilibria: products of several (linear-in-P) factors indicate multiple fixed points (each factor’s zero), suggesting regime shifts between low and high population states.

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4 + c5*P
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function of **P** only; **t** unused):
\[
0.9909642091509507\,(1-\tfrac{P}{39.01184604772507})P\;+\;0.9909642091509507\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.9909642091509507\,P
\]
Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.9909642091509507\,(P-\tfrac{P^2}{39.01184604772507})+0.9909642091509507\,P
= (2\cdot 0.9909642091509507)P - \Big(\tfrac{0.9909642091509507}{39.01184604772507}\Big)P^2
\]
So GT has the form
\[
A\,P^2 + B\,P + C\,P^{1/3}
\]
with \(A\neq 0\), \(B\neq 0\), \(C\neq 0\). It contains a **fractional power \(P^{1/3}\)** and **no rational-in-\(P\)** denominators, no logs/exp/max, and no \(t\)-dependence.

Now check candidates for whether they can be set to exactly \(A P^2 + B P + C P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\).
